        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript.


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

      response:
        output: >-

          Genes coordinate their expression in a concerted manner to execute
          their functions, and understanding how they contribute to complex
          traits requires a comprehensive analysis of gene regulation across
          diverse conditions. Recent studies have demonstrated that elucidating
          the mechanisms of gene expression is essential for developing novel
          therapeutic strategies. Although transcriptome-wide association
          studies have shed light on the role of individual genes in disease
          mechanisms, the latest models suggest that gene-gene interactions play
          a critical role in the development and progression of complex
          diseases. To address this challenge, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
          computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent
          representation, enabling a joint analysis of gene expression patterns
          and drug mechanisms. Our method is based on modules of genes with
          similar expression profiles across relevant conditions, which are
          prioritized based on their functional significance in disease-relevant
          cell types. We observe that PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known
          drug-disease associations and inferences mechanisms of action, as well
          as identifying functionally important players that lack genetic
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules. By
          incorporating co-expressed gene groups, PhenoPLIER offers a novel
          framework for contextualizing genetic associations and revealing
          potential therapeutic targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our
          approach provides a valuable tool for understanding the complex
          interplay between genes and their role in disease etiology and drug
          mechanisms, ultimately facilitating the discovery of new therapeutic
          strategies.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

        display: >-

      vars: *ref_1
      response:
        output: >-

          Genetic studies have shown that complex traits are influenced by
          multiple genes interacting with each other in specific contexts.
          However, understanding how these genes contribute to disease etiology
          and drug mechanisms remains a challenge. Recent advances in functional
          genomics have enabled the study of gene expression patterns across
          different conditions, but integrating this information with genetic
          associations and pharmacological data has been limited. Here we
          introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates
          gene-trait associations and drug perturbation data into a common
          latent representation, leveraging modules of co-expressed genes across
          relevant cell types. Our approach accurately predicts known
          drug-disease pairs and inferences mechanisms of action, and
          prioritizes functionally important players in trait-associated
          modules. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations and
          identifying potential therapeutic targets missed by single-gene
          strategies. Our approach highlights the importance of considering
          gene-gene interactions in understanding disease etiology and drug
          mechanisms, and demonstrates the power of integrating multi-omics data
          to reveal new insights into complex traits.

        output: >-

          Genes work together in specific contexts to perform their functions,
          and understanding how they influence complex traits requires a
          mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation across diverse
          conditions. Developing new therapies benefits from this insight.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have revealed the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, but modern models
          predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease
          origin and progression. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
          approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
          analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
          similar expression patterns across the same conditions. Our approach
          accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of
          action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
          regulation, we found that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic
          associations by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, revealing
          potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies and providing a
          novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through gene
          modules.

      response:
        output: >-

          Genetic studies have shown that complex traits are influenced by
          multiple genes working in concert, but understanding how these genes
          interact to affect disease remains a challenge. Recent advances in
          functional genomics have enabled the study of gene expression patterns
          across different conditions, but integrating this information with
          genetic association data to identify therapeutic targets remains an
          open question. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that combines gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation, enabling a joint analysis of
          gene expression patterns and drug mechanisms. PhenoPLIER identifies
          disease-relevant modules of co-expressed genes and prioritizes
          functionally important players, even in the absence of direct genetic
          associations. Using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we
          demonstrate that PhenoPLIER can identify potential therapeutic targets
          missed by single-gene strategies. Our approach provides a novel
          framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of
          gene modules, highlighting the importance of considering gene-gene
          interactions in drug discovery and personalized medicine.

        output: >-

          Genes work in concert with each other in specific contexts to execute
          their functions. Understanding how these genes contribute to complex
          traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation
          across diverse conditions. This insight is crucial for developing
          novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have uncovered
          the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
          modern models of complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene
          interactions play a critical role in disease origin and progression.
          We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation, facilitating a joint analysis. This
          representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression
          patterns across the same conditions. Our findings show that diseases
          are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
          cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease
          pairs and inferences mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a
          CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discovered that
          functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized
          in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules, contextualizing genetic associations
          and revealing potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. By
          incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER offers a more
          comprehensive understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms,
          highlighting the importance of considering gene-gene interactions in
          the study of complex traits.

          Genetic studies have shown that complex traits are influenced by
          multiple genes acting in concert, but understanding how these genes
          interact to contribute to disease remains a challenge. Functional
          genomics approaches, such as transcriptome-wide association studies,
          have shed light on the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms.
          However, the complexity of gene-gene interactions and their impact on
          disease etiology remain largely unexplored. Here we introduce
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene expression
          patterns, trait associations, and pharmacological perturbation data to
          reveal the underlying mechanisms of disease. By clustering genes into
          modules based on their co-expression across different conditions,
          PhenoPLIER identifies disease-relevant gene modules and predicts
          potential therapeutic targets missed by single-gene strategies. Using
          a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we demonstrate the power
          of PhenoPLIER in prioritizing functionally important players and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Our approach provides a novel
          framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of
          gene modules, opening up new avenues for drug discovery and
          personalized medicine.

          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on

          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

          Genetic studies have shown that complex traits are influenced by
          multiple genes interacting with each other in specific contexts.

          and drug mechanisms remains a challenge. Recent advances in functional
          genomics have enabled the identification of gene-gene interactions and

          integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes
          act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
          functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          The study of genetic associations with complex traits has been greatly
          aided by transcriptome-wide association studies, but the full
          understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms requires a
          deeper comprehension of gene-gene interactions and expression
          regulation across different conditions. PhenoPLIER, a novel
          computational approach presented in this manuscript, addresses this
          knowledge gap by mapping gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a common latent representation, enabling a
          joint analysis that reveals the importance of gene modules and their
          expression patterns in disease mechanisms. By integrating functional
          genomics and gene co-expression data, PhenoPLIER identifies
          trait-associated modules expressed in relevant cell types, which are
          significantly associated with diseases and accurately predicts known
          drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Moreover, the
          approach highlights functionally important players that lack genetic
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules, as
          demonstrated by a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation. The presentation
          of PhenoPLIER offers a framework for projecting genetic associations
          through gene expression patterns, providing new insights into disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms, and advancing the field of functional
          genomics.

          Genetic studies have made significant progress in understanding the
          genetic basis of complex diseases, but the field still lacks a
          comprehensive framework for interpreting genetic associations and
          elucidating disease mechanisms. Functional genomics approaches, such
          as transcriptome-wide association studies (TWAS), have shed light on
          the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
          the complexity of gene-gene interactions and the context-specific
          nature of gene expression remain a challenge for understanding disease
          etiology and identifying therapeutic targets. To address this gap, we
          developed PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation, enabling a joint analysis of gene
          expression patterns and drug mechanisms. Our method prioritizes
          functionally important genes in trait-associated modules and
          identifies potential therapeutic targets missed by single-gene
          strategies. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for contextualizing genetic associations
          and revealing disease mechanisms. Our approach is accurate in
          predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
          action, and we demonstrate its power in a CRISPR screen for lipid
          regulation. PhenoPLIER offers a valuable tool for researchers and
          clinicians to better understand complex diseases and develop effective
          therapies.

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes
          act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
          functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex

          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with

          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          Genetic studies have long sought to uncover the complex relationships
          between genetic variation and disease susceptibility. However, the

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic

          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          In the field of genetics, understanding how genes work together to
          influence complex traits is crucial for developing new therapies.

          across different conditions remains a significant challenge. Our study
          aims to address this gap by projecting genetic associations through

          modules. The broader significance of our findings lies in the

          complex diseases and advance our understanding of drug mechanisms,

          treatments.

          In the field of genetics, understanding the complex interplay between
          genes and their role in disease development remains a significant
          challenge. While genome-wide association studies have identified
          numerous genetic variants associated with diseases, the mechanisms by

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a

          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

          In the field of genetics, understanding the complex interplay between

          Genes function in a concerted manner, working together in specific
          contexts to carry out their roles. Understanding how these genes
          contribute to complex traits requires a comprehensive grasp of
          expression regulation across diverse conditions. This knowledge is
          crucial for the development of novel therapeutic approaches. While
          transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the role of
          individual genes in disease mechanisms, modern models of complex trait
          architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions play a vital role in
          disease origination and progression. To address this challenge, we
          introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent space for joint analysis. This space is based on modules
          of genes with similar expression patterns across various conditions.
          Our approach reveals that diseases are significantly linked to gene
          modules expressed in relevant cell types, and accurately predicts
          known drug-disease pairs while providing insights into mechanism of
          action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to investigate lipid
          regulation, we find that functionally important players lack direct
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER.

          Genes work together in specific contexts to perform their functions,
          but understanding how they influence complex traits requires a deep
          dive into expression regulation across different conditions. This
          knowledge is critical for developing new therapies. Previous studies

          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER, further
          supporting its effectiveness. By filling this gap in our understanding

          novel therapeutic targets and drug repurposing opportunities.

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER.

          Genes work together in specific contexts to perform their functions,
          and understanding how they influence complex traits requires a
          mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation across diverse
          conditions. Although transcriptome-wide association studies have
          revealed the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms,
          modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role
          in disease origin and progression. To address this gap, we introduce
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis. This representation relies
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same

          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER, highlighting its ability to identify potential therapeutic
          targets. By bridging the gap between gene co-expression and drug
          mechanisms, PhenoPLIER offers a powerful tool for understanding
          disease etiology and identifying novel therapeutic strategies.

          In the field of genetics, understanding the complex interplay between
          genes and their role in disease etiology is crucial for developing
          effective therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have
          shed light on the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms, the
          modern paradigm suggests that gene-gene interactions play a vital role

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER.

          Genes coordinate their functions in specific contexts, and
          understanding how they contribute to complex traits requires a
          mechanistic grasp of expression regulation across diverse conditions.
          This insight is crucial for developing novel therapies, as

          Revised abstract:


          Uncovering the genetic basis of complex traits requires a
          comprehensive understanding of gene expression patterns and their
          relationship to disease mechanisms. PhenoPLIER, our novel
          computational approach, maps gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation,
          enabling a joint analysis of gene expression patterns and drug
          mechanisms. By integrating modules of genes with similar expression
          patterns across relevant conditions, PhenoPLIER identifies significant
          associations between diseases and gene modules expressed in specific
          cell types. Our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs
          and inferences mechanisms of action, as demonstrated by a CRISPR
          screen for lipid regulation. PhenoPLIER prioritizes functionally
          important players in trait-associated modules, providing new insights
          into disease etiology and therapeutic targets. This study highlights
          the potential of PhenoPLIER for identifying novel drug mechanisms and
          repurposing drugs for complex diseases.

              Genes coordinate their expression in a concerted manner to execute
              their functions, and understanding how they contribute to complex

              complex interplay between genes and their role in disease etiology
              and drug mechanisms, ultimately facilitating the discovery of new
              therapeutic strategies.

            text: >-

              Genetic studies have shown that complex traits are influenced by
              multiple genes working in concert, but understanding how these
              genes interact to affect disease remains a challenge. Recent
              advances in functional genomics have enabled the study of gene
              expression patterns across different conditions, but integrating
              this information with genetic association data to identify
              therapeutic targets remains an open question. Here, we introduce
              PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that combines gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
              latent representation, enabling a joint analysis of gene
              expression patterns and drug mechanisms. PhenoPLIER identifies
              disease-relevant modules of co-expressed genes and prioritizes
              functionally important players, even in the absence of direct
              genetic associations. Using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we demonstrate that PhenoPLIER can identify potential
              therapeutic targets missed by single-gene strategies. Our approach
              provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules, highlighting the importance of
              considering gene-gene interactions in drug discovery and
              personalized medicine.

              Genes work in concert with each other in specific contexts to
              execute their functions. Understanding how these genes contribute

            text: >-

              Genetic studies have shown that complex traits are influenced by
              multiple genes acting in concert, but understanding how these
              genes interact to contribute to disease remains a challenge.
              Functional genomics approaches, such as transcriptome-wide
              association studies, have shed light on the role of individual
              genes in disease mechanisms. However, the complexity of gene-gene
              interactions and their impact on disease etiology remain largely
              unexplored. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
              that integrates gene expression patterns, trait associations, and
              pharmacological perturbation data to reveal the underlying
              mechanisms of disease. By clustering genes into modules based on
              their co-expression across different conditions, PhenoPLIER
              identifies disease-relevant gene modules and predicts potential
              therapeutic targets missed by single-gene strategies. Using a
              CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we demonstrate the
              power of PhenoPLIER in prioritizing functionally important players
              and inferring mechanisms of action. Our approach provides a novel
              framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens
              of gene modules, opening up new avenues for drug discovery and
              personalized medicine.

              The study of gene expression patterns and their relationship to
              complex traits has been a longstanding challenge in genetics
              research. While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed
              light on the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms,
              modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial

              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for joint analysis. This

              expression patterns across the same conditions, which are

              approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
              inferences mechanisms of action, and a CRISPR screen analysis of
              lipid regulation reveals functionally important players that lack
              associations but are prioritized by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion,
              PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations through the lens of gene modules, revealing potential
              targets missed by single-gene strategies and advancing our
              understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              understanding of expression regulation across different
              conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical for
              developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
              have helped uncover the role of individual genes in
              disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
              architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
              play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we
              introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for a joint analysis. This
              representation is base on modules of genes with similar expression
              patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are
              significantl associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed genes,
              PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,

              provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules.

              Genetic studies have shown that complex traits are influenced by
              multiple genes interacting with each other in specific contexts.
              However, understanding how these genes contribute to disease
              etiology and drug mechanisms remains a challenge. Recent advances
              in functional genomics have enabled the identification of
              gene-gene interactions and their role in disease origin and
              progression. Yet, there is a need for a computational approach
              that integrates gene expression patterns, genetic associations,
              and pharmacological data to provide a comprehensive understanding
              of disease mechanisms. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel
              method that maps gene-trait associations and drug perturbation
              data into a common latent representation, allowing for a joint
              analysis of gene expression patterns and their relationship to
              disease and drug mechanisms. By grouping genes into modules based
              on their co-expression patterns across different conditions,
              PhenoPLIER identifies disease-associated modules that are enriched
              in relevant cell types. Our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and inferences mechanisms of action. Moreover,
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we demonstrate
              that PhenoPLIER prioritizes functionally important genes in
              trait-associated modules, highlighting potential therapeutic
              targets missed by single-gene strategies. In conclusion,
              PhenoPLIER provides a framework for projecting genetic
              associations through gene expression patterns, revealing novel
              drug targets and advancing our understanding of disease etiology
              and drug mechanisms.

              Genetic studies have made significant progress in understanding
              the genetic basis of complex diseases, but the field still lacks a
              comprehensive framework for interpreting genetic associations and
              elucidating disease mechanisms. Functional genomics approaches,
              such as transcriptome-wide association studies (TWAS), have shed
              light on the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
              mechanisms. However, the complexity of gene-gene interactions and
              the context-specific nature of gene expression remain a challenge
              for understanding disease etiology and identifying therapeutic
              targets. To address this gap, we developed PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation, enabling a joint analysis of gene expression
              patterns and drug mechanisms. Our method prioritizes functionally
              important genes in trait-associated modules and identifies
              potential therapeutic targets missed by single-gene strategies. By
              incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER provides a
              novel framework for contextualizing genetic associations and
              revealing disease mechanisms. Our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action, and we demonstrate its power in a CRISPR screen for lipid
              regulation. PhenoPLIER offers a valuable tool for researchers and
              clinicians to better understand complex diseases and develop
              effective therapies.

              suggests that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in

              PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
              latent representation, enabling a joint analysis of gene
              expression patterns and drug mechanisms. Our method is based on
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across relevant
              conditions, which are significantly associated with diseases and
              accurately predict known drug-disease pairs. Moreover, using a
              CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we demonstrate that
              PhenoPLIER can prioritize functionally important players missed by
              single-gene strategies. By incorporating groups of co-expressed
              genes, PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for contextualizing
              genetic associations and revealing potential therapeutic targets.
              Our approach provides a significant improvement over traditional
              methods, which often rely on single-gene analysis, and paves the
              way for more effective drug development and personalized medicine.

              Genetic studies have long sought to uncover the complex
              relationships between genetic variation and disease
              susceptibility. However, the identification of genetic
              associations has been limited by a lack of understanding of how
              genes interact with each other to modulate trait expression.
              Functional genomics approaches, such as transcriptome-wide
              association studies, have provided valuable insights into the role
              of individual genes in disease mechanisms. Yet, the complexity of
              gene-gene interactions and their contribution to disease origin
              and progression remain unclear. To address this gap, we introduce
              PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene
              expression patterns with pharmacological perturbation data to
              identify modules of co-expressed genes associated with disease
              traits. By prioritizing functional players in trait-associated
              modules, PhenoPLIER reveals potential therapeutic targets missed
              by single-gene strategies. Our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and inferences mechanisms of action, providing
              a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through
              the lens of gene modules. PhenoPLIER highlights the importance of
              considering gene-gene interactions in understanding disease
              etiology and identifying therapeutic targets, advancing our
              understanding of complex traits and their treatment.

              In the field of genetics and functional genomics, understanding
              the complex relationships between gene expression patterns and
              disease etiology remains a significant challenge. While
              transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the role

              interactions with genomic data to identify potential therapeutic
              targets remains an open question. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. By incorporating modules of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. Our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease
              pairs and inferences mechanisms of action, and we demonstrate its
              utility in a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation. In conclusion,
              PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations through the lens of gene modules, advancing our
              understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms and opening
              up new avenues for therapeutic target identification.

            text: >-

              In the field of genetics, understanding the complex relationships
              between gene expression and disease etiology remains a significant
              challenge. While recent advances in genomics have enabled the
              identification of genetic associations with diseases, the
              mechanistic understanding of these associations remains limited.
              In this study, we aim to fill this gap by developing a novel
              approach called PhenoPLIER, which integrates gene co-expression
              and functional genomics to project genetic associations onto
              disease etiology and drug mechanisms. Our approach is based on the
              idea that genes acting in concert with each other in specific
              contexts are critical for understanding expression regulation and
              its relationship to complex traits. By incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. We evaluated the accuracy of PhenoPLIER using a CRISPR
              screen to analyze lipid regulation and found that functionally
              important players lack associations but are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules. Our results show that diseases are
              significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Overall,
              PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations through the lens of gene modules, advancing our
              understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms, and paving
              the way for the development of new therapeutic strategies.

              In the field of genetics, understanding how genes work together to

              In the field of genetics, understanding the complex interplay
              between genes and their role in disease development is crucial for
              identifying new therapeutic targets. While genetic studies have
              identified numerous associations between specific genes and
              diseases, the mechanisms by which these genes contribute to
              disease remain unclear. Functional genomics approaches, such as
              gene co-expression analysis, have the potential to provide
              valuable insights into these mechanisms. However, existing methods
              often focus on single genes, overlooking the coordinated action of
              gene modules. Our study aims to address this gap by developing
              PhenoPLIER, a novel approach that integrates gene expression
              patterns and prioritizes functionally important players in
              trait-associated modules. By contextualizing genetic associations
              within gene modules, PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Using a CRISPR
              screen to analyze lipid regulation, we demonstrate that PhenoPLIER
              can identify potential targets missed by single-gene strategies.
              Our results highlight the power of incorporating gene modules in
              genetic association studies, providing a novel framework for
              interpreting genetic associations and identifying new therapeutic
              targets.

              communicate to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The first
              sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
              which the particular research is situated. Then, this context is
              narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
              answered. A successful context section sets the stage for
              distinguishing the paper’s contributions from the current state of
              the art by communicating what is missing in the literature (i.e.,
              the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e., the connection
              between the specific gap and the broader context that the paper
              opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question. Then
              you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
              Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the
              question that was posed at the end of the context section. There
              is often a second part to the conclusion section that highlights
              how this conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e.,
              "broader significance").

              framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens

              In the field of genetics, understanding the complex interplay
              between genes and their role in disease etiology is crucial for
              developing effective therapies. While transcriptome-wide
              association studies have shed light on the role of individual

              gene-gene interactions and their relationship to disease
              mechanisms, our approach offers a valuable tool for drug discovery
              and repurposing, and sheds light on the complex genetic
              architecture underlying multifactorial diseases.

              progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint

              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.

              In the field of genetics, understanding how genes work together to

              While transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover
              the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms,
              modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a critical

              therapeutic strategies.

              necessary to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the
              abstract must follow the following structure: 1) The context must
              communicate to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The first
              sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
              which the particular research is situated. Then, this context is
              narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
              answered. A successful context section sets the stage for
              distinguishing the paper’s contributions from the current state of
              the art by communicating what is missing in the literature (i.e.,
              the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e., the connection
              between the specific gap and the broader context that the paper
              opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question. Then
              you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
              Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the
              question that was posed at the end of the context section. There
              is often a second part to the conclusion section that highlights
              how this conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e.,
              "broader significance").

              ---


              Genes coordinate their functions in specific contexts, and
              understanding how they contribute to complex traits requires a
              mechanistic grasp of expression regulation across diverse
              conditions. This insight is crucial for developing novel
              therapies, as demonstrated by previous studies. While
              transcriptome-wide association studies have revealed the role of
              individual genes in disease-related mechanisms, modern models
              suggest that gene-gene interactions play a key role in disease
              origins and progression. To address this challenge, we present
              PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
              latent representation, enabling a joint analysis. This
              representation is based on modules of genes with similar
              expression patterns across the same conditions. Our findings
              indicate that diseases are significantly linked to gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately
              predicts known drug-disease pairs and inferences mechanisms of
              action. Notably, a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation reveals that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.


              Revised abstract:


              Uncovering the genetic basis of complex traits requires a
              comprehensive understanding of gene expression patterns and their
              relationship to disease mechanisms. PhenoPLIER, our novel
              computational approach, maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation, enabling a joint analysis of gene expression
              patterns and drug mechanisms. By integrating modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across relevant conditions, PhenoPLIER
              identifies significant associations between diseases and gene
              modules expressed in specific cell types. Our approach accurately
              predicts known drug-disease pairs and inferences mechanisms of
              action, as demonstrated by a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation.
              PhenoPLIER prioritizes functionally important players in
              trait-associated modules, providing new insights into disease
              etiology and therapeutic targets. This study highlights the
              potential of PhenoPLIER for identifying novel drug mechanisms and
              repurposing drugs for complex diseases.

              Genes work together in specific contexts to perform their
              functions, but understanding how they influence complex traits
              requires a deep dive into expression regulation across different
              conditions. This knowledge is critical for developing new
              therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have
              uncovered the role of individual genes in disease-relevant

              our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
              inferences mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen
              to analyze lipid regulation, we discovered that functionally
              important players lack associations but are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER, highlighting the power of
              our approach in identifying potential therapeutic targets. By
              filling this gap in our understanding of complex traits, our
              research opens up new avenues for drug repurposing and clustering
              of complex traits, advancing the field of functional genomics.
